    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText2687078990213326632" style="display:none">According to ancient Black Forest legend, on the Night of the Seventh Moon, Loke, the God of Mischief, is at large in the world. It is a night for festivity and joyful celebration. It is a night for singing and dancing. And it is a night for love.<br /><br />Helena Trant was enchanted by everything she found in the Black Forest -- especially its legends. But then, on the Night of the Seventh Moon, she started to live one of them, and the enchantment turned suddenly into a terrifying nightmare . . .</span>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_7015882').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

    I'm not sure what your question is? Is it how they showed her a baby's body when hers was not dead? The baby she saw belonged to the girl she talked t<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I'm not sure what your question is? Is it how they showed her a baby's body when hers was not dead? The baby she saw belonged to the girl she talked to earlier. They told Helena that the girl had died and that her baby was a little boy who was taken in buy the girl's grandmother. Actually the girl lived and her baby girl was the one who died. Helena's little boy was taken away.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8840901731703220751">I read nearly all of Victoria Holt's books, but this was by far my favorite. I still remember the excitement of the mystery and love story. I just recently ordered my own copy to read it again. Her books have clean romance they are a simplified version of the types of stories Jane Austin writes. They often have a lower class girl/governess who falls in love with someone out of her league. There is often a mystery of murder or kidnapping to go along with it. They are set in castles or on the moor</span>
  <span id="freeText8840901731703220751" style="display:none">I read nearly all of Victoria Holt's books, but this was by far my favorite. I still remember the excitement of the mystery and love story. I just recently ordered my own copy to read it again. Her books have clean romance they are a simplified version of the types of stories Jane Austin writes. They often have a lower class girl/governess who falls in love with someone out of her league. There is often a mystery of murder or kidnapping to go along with it. They are set in castles or on the moor's with fancy dresses and parties. They are just fun easy books to entertain yourself. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8642441099874108914">Aww yeah, 1970s Victoria Holt. This was the sort of thing I read with abandon in my impressionable late middle/early high school years, and is probably to blame for my deep lingering affection for anything gothic-tinged. This book has some issues--repetition of certain phrases and themes, and characters who are too stupid to live, mainly--but if you cut it some slack, it's thoroughly enjoyable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2111070082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2111070082" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2111070082?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8270967-on-the-night-of-the-seventh-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=2017-library-love-challenge">2017-library-love-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=halloween-bingo-2017">halloween-bingo-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111070082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6841546309608787803">I read this for "Gothic square". "On the Night of the Seventh Moon" by Victoria Holt.<br/><br/>So I just realized after finishing this book that I really can't write a very in-depth review, because if I do I'll be spoiling the entire book. So I'm going to try to keep this to just general things and then you can make a decision if you want to read this for Halloween book bingo.<br/><br/>On the night of the seventh moon is told from the first person point of view of a young girl named Helena. Helena is raised in a lo</span>
  <span id="freeText6841546309608787803" style="display:none">I read this for "Gothic square". "On the Night of the Seventh Moon" by Victoria Holt.<br /><br />So I just realized after finishing this book that I really can't write a very in-depth review, because if I do I'll be spoiling the entire book. So I'm going to try to keep this to just general things and then you can make a decision if you want to read this for Halloween book bingo.<br /><br />On the night of the seventh moon is told from the first person point of view of a young girl named Helena. Helena is raised in a loving household, the only fly in the ointment so to speak is the fact that her parents are both desperately in love with each other and that doesn't leave a lot of love left over for her when they are in the same room together.<br /><br />Helena's mother is from a Germanic country. The book doesn't really come out and say where she's from exactly and I couldn't guess and I was honestly not really in the mood to go do some digging about this. Helena's father is English and though many around them don't think the marriage is going to work, it does.<br /><br />The only thing that Helena's mother really wanted was for her daughter to be sent away to learn Germany and French and other things and Helena is eventually sent to a boarding school that's near a town that her mother knows. So we find out pretty early on that Helena is sent away from home for four years and is being raised and taught by nuns.<br /><br />Everything kind of goes sideways for Helena when she gets lost in a forest when mist suddenly forms. Helena meets some mysterious man and she calls him Siegfried. He takes her back to his lodge (as one does) and then goes about trying to seduce her. Long story short, everyone around can tell that Siegfried is up to no good, but Helena feels so excited by things. Blech. This little adventure ends up with her almost being raped (she bolts the door and is later awoken by the doorknob turning) but in the light of day is disappointed. <br /><br />Smack upside the head for Helena.<br /><br />Cue Helena having to go home after her mother passes away and then her father does as well. Being forced to go home to her dreary little village and not be able to see her Siegfried again it's just making her sad. I on the other hand think that if she had any sense she would realize that Siegfried was not a cool dude and she should just move on but then we wouldn't have a story here if that's what the author chose to do what do we?<br /><br />Fast forward to some relatives of Helena's mother showing up and when she's given the opportunity to return with them to be at a nearby Village that is close to her old school she jumps on it because of course all she's thinking of is seeing her Siegfried again.<br /><br />And see him again she does. I'm not going to talk much after that because that's where the mystery lies and the entire rest of the book is Helena unraveling who's being truthful and who is lying to her. I do have to say that even when she does find out what's been going on I think that she took things way too laid-back for for what I would have probably have done. And I honestly wish that Holt had just decided to end the book in a different way because I never did warm up to Siegfried.<br /><br />I have to say that I thought that the writing that Holt did in this one was very good. I love the descriptions of the town's and other locations that appear in this story. Holt really made me feel like I was Helena in a couple scenes as she becomes more and more thrilled with her surroundings. Everything sounds positively Gothic at times which was nice to read on an overcast day. <br /><br />The ending just turned into a mess though. Once again won't spoil for others, but it just didn't make a lot of sense at all. Then Holt does an epilogue that shows what happened to everyone and I ended up just feeling dissatisfied. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6841546309608787803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7224684694072953918" style="display:none"><i>"Sometimes, looking back, I ask myself: Why did you accept this and that? <div id="review_1385662215" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1385662215" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1385662215?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=stereotypical">stereotypical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=too-predictable">too-predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=formulaic">formulaic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1385662215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3327351314309151523">While Victoria Holt's formulaic historical romance stories certainly were fun enough and even rather delightful when I was reading them as a teenager, even then, even at that time, I did already notice that with regard to settings and thematics, Holt does seem to do a much better job and to present a more believable, less stereotypical and generally also sufficiently realistic sense of time and place when she locates her tales in the United Kingdom and not abroad. <br/><br/>For yes indeed, when I read Vic</span>
  <span id="freeText3327351314309151523" style="display:none">While Victoria Holt's formulaic historical romance stories certainly were fun enough and even rather delightful when I was reading them as a teenager, even then, even at that time, I did already notice that with regard to settings and thematics, Holt does seem to do a much better job and to present a more believable, less stereotypical and generally also sufficiently realistic sense of time and place when she locates her tales in the United Kingdom and not abroad. <br /><br />For yes indeed, when I read Victoria Holt's 1972 novel <u>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</u> in 1984, while many of her descriptions of the German forest did kind of feel authentic and descriptively believable (even though they at times also rather reminded me of travel and tourist brochures touting the natural splendours of the Black Forest, of the Schwarzwald), the entire plot of <u>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</u> did (to teenaged me) not only feel full, full, full to the absolute brim with Holt's to be expected historical romance formulas, reading <u>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</u> also felt very strongly (and most annoyingly I might add) like I was reading a typical "German" fairy tale and one where ALL of the heroes and ALL of the villains were so woefully predictable and stereotypical that my perusal very quickly became rather a tedious and often a bit frustrating reading slog (and yes, where in particular the vast majority of the German characters were depicted by Victoria Holt as rather caricature like at best and certainly with much less nuance and depth than her English characters, such as for example her main protagonist Helena Trant). <br /><br />And while at the age of seventeen, I was actually still only partially and thus not absolutely annoyed and frustrated with and by this (even if it did make me as a person of German background more than a trifle uncomfortable), the entire English schoolgirl meets Southern German prince in the forest and ends up marrying him scenario (only to have the couple separated by politics and evil machinations) has been upon rereading <u>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</u> not only (and as to be expected) too fairy and folktale like for my reading tastes, but yes, I personally also do think that Victoria Holt is presenting some rather problematic anti-German and especially anti-German politics attitudes in <u>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</u> (since the German individuals who are bent on keeping Helena and her princely lover/husband apart are ALL in my humble opinion depicted and presented by the author, by Victoria Holt as being pretty much total über-villain typecasts with major doses of rabid nationalism, as "persons" who are stereotypical politics and dynastics above everything nasties).</span>
  <a data-text-id="3327351314309151523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <b>And I had learned the truth of what happened on the Night of the Seventh Moon; I had taken back those six days of my life; they belonged to me and I had been wantonly deceived.</b>

Helena starts off as a young girl going to school in Germany, she gets lost wandering in the woods and gets "rescued" by a man.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56785906" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1735763-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442495481p2/1735763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56785906?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1735763-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56785906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer961377103412462887">I picked up an old copy of this book for $0.25 the other day when I dropped off some items at my local donation centre. The pages were yellowed and the writing small but the topic intrigued me. It's been many years since I last read Victoria Holt, an author known as "the supreme writer of the 'gothic' romance".<br/><br/>Mystery, suspense, mystical forests, dark foreboding castles, trickery and folklore legends together with interesting characters made this book a very good read.<br/><br/>The story is told from Hele</span>
  <span id="freeText961377103412462887" style="display:none">I picked up an old copy of this book for $0.25 the other day when I dropped off some items at my local donation centre. The pages were yellowed and the writing small but the topic intrigued me. It's been many years since I last read Victoria Holt, an author known as "the supreme writer of the 'gothic' romance".<br /><br />Mystery, suspense, mystical forests, dark foreboding castles, trickery and folklore legends together with interesting characters made this book a very good read.<br /><br />The story is told from Helena Trant, the heroine's point of view as she recaps her past, a past shrouded in mystery as she tries to uncover exactly what happened to her on the night of the seventh moon — when a festival celebration of mischief took place. She is rescued by a handsome stranger with whom she strongly believes to have fallen in love and subsequently married, only to wake up to a psychological nightmare of being told it had been all a dream and none of it had happened.<br /><br />The mystery deepens as we speed through the pages to uncover what really happened. Some of it is predictable, but the plot is well laid out and we are continuously kept guessing regarding the different characters as to whether they are truly Helena's friend or her enemy. Although the heroine's character is well developed, I found the hero's was not. I should have liked their relationship to have been explored a little more.<br /><br />However, if you are looking for a good gothic romance this book delivers.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="961377103412462887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36187503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7042473035468890868">I first read this book probably fifteen years ago. It has been my favorite Victoria Holt book ever since--and yes, I have read all 32 books she penned under that name. To tell anything about this would be to give too much away so I'll just say this: The romance was breathtaking; the action was, in a way, believable; and the intrigue was shocking. For those of you who need a basic description, here's what the back of the book says:<br/><br/>On the Night of the Seventh Moon, according to ancient Black Fores</span>
  <span id="freeText7042473035468890868" style="display:none">I first read this book probably fifteen years ago. It has been my favorite Victoria Holt book ever since--and yes, I have read all 32 books she penned under that name. To tell anything about this would be to give too much away so I'll just say this: The romance was breathtaking; the action was, in a way, believable; and the intrigue was shocking. For those of you who need a basic description, here's what the back of the book says:<br /><br />On the Night of the Seventh Moon, according to ancient Black Forest legend, Loke, the God of Mischief, was abroad in the world. It was a night for festivity and joyful celebration. It was a night for singing and dancing. And it was a night for love.<br /><br />Helena Trant was enchanted by everything she found in the Black Forest--its people, its mysterious castles, its legends and lore. Especially its legends of love.<br /><br />Until, one day, she started to live one of them and the enchantment turned suddenly into a terrifying nightmare....</span>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=exotic-locale">exotic-locale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035539398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16578468930527852634">Love and Mystery in the Black Forest!<br/><br/>Set in Germany and England from 1859 to 1870 (with an end note in 1901), this tells the story of Helena Trant whose parents were so much in love they had little time for her. Still, hers was a happy childhood among books in Oxford where her father had a bookstore. When she was old enough, her parents sent her to Germany near the Black Forest to a convent school where her mother had been educated.<br/><br/>Helena loves the forest and the fairy tales surrounding it. She </span>
  <span id="freeText16578468930527852634" style="display:none">Love and Mystery in the Black Forest!<br /><br />Set in Germany and England from 1859 to 1870 (with an end note in 1901), this tells the story of Helena Trant whose parents were so much in love they had little time for her. Still, hers was a happy childhood among books in Oxford where her father had a bookstore. When she was old enough, her parents sent her to Germany near the Black Forest to a convent school where her mother had been educated.<br /><br />Helena loves the forest and the fairy tales surrounding it. She hears of the legend of the night of the seventh moon “when mischief is abroad and is routed with the coming of dawn.” On one night, she gets lost in the mist of the forest and is rescued by a man who takes her to his hunting lodge. She taken with him that she might have allowed him to have his way with her but for the intervention of a housekeeper who took measures to preserve Helena’s virtue. But Helena never forgot the man even though she did not know his name.<br /><br />Years later, she returns to Germany and on another night of the seventh moon Helena meets and marries her German at his hunting lodge, but then she wakes from her idyllic honeymoon to discover she has been drugged by a physician who tells her she has escaped a horror that befell her in the forest. Helena lives in a fog of dreams and wonders where truth is.<br /><br />I have to say that I love Holt’s writing, and this story sucked me in immediately. It is labeled as a romantic suspense, but I didn’t see it containing any more suspense than many historical romances. But it does have a Gothic feel and there is a mystery. Holt had me wondering what had really happened. She did an excellent job of that. The book is a bit slow in the middle, and the hero and heroine are separated for years. In that interim, I found passages that seemed repetitive, but the ending is a great one. As always, Holt is a master storyteller and creates wonderfully vivid characters. Despite the slower middle, I recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16578468930527852634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11220878366279049038" style="display:none">This was a reread for me for bookclub. I originally read this as a teenager back in the 1970s. It was just as readable this second time through. I didn't remember much of the plot even though I remembered vaguely that the book ended happily. I did feel the angst at the horrible things that were happening to Helena. I probably figured out what was going on earlier this time since I've read so many books since I first read this but it was all new the first time through and as a teenager I wasn't quite so savvy. Still the writing was such that you kept wanting to read to find out for sure what was going on and to get Helena through the bad stuff.<br /><br />It is of course a gothic novel so even though there is a romance the main thrust of the story is the surreal things that are happening to the poor heroine. A fun read altogether.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14793931174550393270"><i>Gothic romance for the win XD!<br/>Dunno, when I read this book, way back when (six years to be precise anyway) I was thrilled by the time period most of Victoria Holt's books took place in. Beautiful dresses and parties, eerie castle settings, English landscapes, etc, etc, etc.<br/><br/>I don't remember this book a whole lot. I just remember a story, a legend, a mystery, a love, and poor character development (especially on the hero, Maximillian, side). I also remember I was terrified for Helena's fate becaus</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14793931174550393270" style="display:none"><i>Gothic romance for the win XD!<br />Dunno, when I read this book, way back when (six years to be precise anyway) I was thrilled by the time period most of Victoria Holt's books took place in. Beautiful dresses and parties, eerie castle settings, English landscapes, etc, etc, etc.<br /><br />I don't remember this book a whole lot. I just remember a story, a legend, a mystery, a love, and poor character development (especially on the hero, Maximillian, side). I also remember I was terrified for Helena's fate because she was asked to spend the night in a castle with a complete and total stranger she found in the forest. The charming stranger took her to the castle after she was lured into the forest and twisted her ankle (or something) and was invited to his humble residence (a castle in the middle of a forest). <br /><br />Anyway, there was a scene in which she locks the door of her room because the servant of the man advised her to do so. And in the middle of the night she could hear the door knob turning as if somebody wanted to come in. Spooky and scary man! This passage is the one I remember most of the book because Holt described every little detail of fear and apprehension of it. I was as nervous and scared as Helena. And most of the time I thought her foolish for the irrational decisions she made when first encounter by this stranger. <br /><br />But anyway. I felt Helena had some character development through the book, but I cannot say the same thing for Maximillian. He was just so plain and systematic.<br /><br />Overall, this is a pretty easy and enjoyable read. If you like gothic, kind of Victorian-ish romance, you should definitely check this book out.<i></i></i></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219093040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3367721216127768219">Bottom line: this is a fun hairdryer book. Don't expect too much of it, and you'll be pleased.<br/><br/>On the Night of the Seventh Moon tells the tale of Helena Trant, the daughter of an English man and a German woman, who grows up in Oxford in the late 1800s, listening to her mother’s tales of the dark German forest where she was educated. When Helena is fourteen, she, too, is sent to be educated at the same seminary on the edge of the forest.<br/><br/>At the age of eighteen, Helena has lost her mother and is app</span>
  <span id="freeText3367721216127768219" style="display:none">Bottom line: this is a fun hairdryer book. Don't expect too much of it, and you'll be pleased.<br /><br />On the Night of the Seventh Moon tells the tale of Helena Trant, the daughter of an English man and a German woman, who grows up in Oxford in the late 1800s, listening to her mother’s tales of the dark German forest where she was educated. When Helena is fourteen, she, too, is sent to be educated at the same seminary on the edge of the forest.<br /><br />At the age of eighteen, Helena has lost her mother and is approaching the end of her time in the Lokenwald (Loki’s Forest). On a picnic with a nun and several fellow students, she gets separated from her classmates when a thick fog arises. She is rescued by a tall, handsome man on a beautiful horse, who, amused by her pluck and feistiness, takes her back to his hunting lodge and gives her supper. The intervention of a kindly housekeeper saves her virtue, for (OMG ENORMOUS SPOILER ALERT!!!) the man is a bit of a rake.<br /><br />The next day, Helena returns to the seminary, and shortly after that, the death of her father calls her back home to Oxford. But she never forgets her rescuer, though she knows what his intent was.<br /><br />A few years later, a cousin of her mother’s finds her in Oxford and offers to take her back to live in the Lokenwald again. Helena accepts, though she knows there is only a slight chance of meeting her rescuer again...<br /><br />Yeah, ok, so you know they’re going to reunite and get married. But you don’t know HOW, do you? Read the book and find out. It’s a fun read.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780449235683" href="/book/show/1250999.On_the_Night_of_the_Seventh_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445433417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12511863971383731193">I ended up liking this a surprising amount. Not even really as a romance--the hero is gone from it so long, and isn't all that vivid. More as a development of the heroine, who suffers a lot, insists on believing her truth, and finally ends up happy. And the setting is beautiful. It all felt way more meaty than <i>The Time of the Hunter's Moon</i>, which I read a few weeks ago, as if Holt had started phoning it in by the time she wrote the latter.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1894200525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894200525" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3146514-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392467433p2/3146514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894200525?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/3146514-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8270967-on-the-night-of-the-seventh-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3146514-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3146514-michael?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3146514-michael?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3146514-michael?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894200525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16326887993152402515">My (admittedly limited) experiences with Victoria Holt have been very uneven. The first book (<i>The Silk Vendetta</i>) did not impress me, but <i>Mistress of Mellyn</i> and <i>Bride of Pendorric</i> were both enjoyable. <i>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</i> falls somewhere between the dull <i>Silk Vendetta</i> and the more interesting "Cornish Gothics"-- nothing anywhere near approximating "brilliant", but also not <i>quite</i> as plodding as <i>Silk Vendetta</i>.<br/><br/>Though I suppose I'll award it three out of five stars, the third is rather gr</span>
  <span id="freeText16326887993152402515" style="display:none">My (admittedly limited) experiences with Victoria Holt have been very uneven. The first book (<i>The Silk Vendetta</i>) did not impress me, but <i>Mistress of Mellyn</i> and <i>Bride of Pendorric</i> were both enjoyable. <i>On the Night of the Seventh Moon</i> falls somewhere between the dull <i>Silk Vendetta</i> and the more interesting "Cornish Gothics"-- nothing anywhere near approximating "brilliant", but also not <i>quite</i> as plodding as <i>Silk Vendetta</i>.<br /><br />Though I suppose I'll award it three out of five stars, the third is rather grudgingly given, as I found myself disliking most of the characters and (more often than not) wishing the book would just hurry up and come to its conclusion. It felt long, which means it was boring me instead of whisking me away from reality, as a good book should do. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the romance is very thin, and the "hero" is a handsome, lust-filled cardboard cut-out-- not very interesting. The heroine, Helena, isn't much better. You get to know her more as a character than you do Maximilian, I suppose, but-- but-- she's just so darn stupid! There are so many times that Helena should pick up on things, but she just won't/can't... Toward the end of the story, the Count says to her, "You are not your usual clever self today." Well, <i>that</i> was a delicious bit of unintentional comedy!<br /><br />I'll probably continue to read Holt, as the mood strikes me, but I'm wary. The quality varies wildly from one book to the next. This one, for me, was closer to the "dud" end of the scale.<br /><br /><br /><b>Specifics (with SPOILERS):</b> <br />--Different times and all that, but it's just so gross when the male characters in a so-called romance are <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[trashy philanderers who have fathered children with multiple women. When Frau Graben fills Helena in on all the dirty details of the Count's history with women, it's clear that Maximilian has a similarly icky past. ("My dear Miss Trant, he[the Count]'s only following the tradition. They've always been for the women. They see them, they fancy them and there's no holding them back. If there are results they don't mind and nor do the women.") Maximilian apparently hasn't been quite so cruel or duplicitous in his dealings with women, but it's still not appealing in a hero. <br /><br />--After all the drama about how Maximilian couldn't just publicly declare his marriage to Helena because it could ignite a war between the principalities (or whatever the heck they were-- forgive my lack of knowledge or interest in German history)-- after all <i>that</i>, the extremely delicate situation is handled neatly and tidily in a single paragraph. "The Prince of Klarenbock, to whom Maximilian had told the whole story during his visit there, behaved magnanimously." ...Well, how convenient. The supposedly serious threat of the people revolting against Maximilian goes "poof", too. Everything is hunky-dory, because there was a war with France-- and war heals all wounds (or something).<br /><br />--Even richer, Maximilian's fancy fake wife gets tossed into a convent to atone for her sins, while her son with Maximilian is raised in the big, happy family Maximilian and Helena create. Ah yes, I'm sure <i>that</i> was never the least little bit awkward, and I'm <i>positive</i> that the son who had been raised for (eight?) years to believe he was "royalty" was now perfectly fine with his new position as an illegitimate son whose father never really loved his mother-- while said mother is apparently whisked out of his life without so much as a backward glance. Good times. <br /><br />Okay, I'll grant you that much of the tension <i>would</i> be washed away by the fact that Maximilian's position is no longer nearly so powerful, by the end of the book. There's not so much of a grand inheritance or position of power to bicker (or hatch murderous plots) over-- otherwise, I would've predicted trouble from Dagobert, who also becomes a part of Helena's Perfect Family (along with Liesel). <br /><br />...But still, even in the humblest of homes, wouldn't there be a certain amount of bitterness in such a truly weird "blended family"? "Mom always liked you best" on steroids! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16326887993152402515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_732821976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732821976" />
    <a title="Regan Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker"><img alt="Regan Walker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442636914p2/7363897.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732821976?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan Walker" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker">Regan Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8270967-on-the-night-of-the-seventh-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=exotic-locale">exotic-locale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732821976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5421274472896597754">Love and Mystery in the Black Forest!<br/><br/>Set in Germany and England from 1859 to 1870 (with an end note in 1901), this tells the story of Helena Trant whose parents were so much in love they had little time for her. Still, hers was a happy childhood among books in Oxford where her father had a bookstore. When she was old enough, her parents sent her to Germany near the Black Forest to a convent school where her mother had been educated.<br/><br/>Helena loves the forest and the fairy tales surrounding it. She </span>
  <span id="freeText5421274472896597754" style="display:none">Love and Mystery in the Black Forest!<br /><br />Set in Germany and England from 1859 to 1870 (with an end note in 1901), this tells the story of Helena Trant whose parents were so much in love they had little time for her. Still, hers was a happy childhood among books in Oxford where her father had a bookstore. When she was old enough, her parents sent her to Germany near the Black Forest to a convent school where her mother had been educated.<br /><br />Helena loves the forest and the fairy tales surrounding it. She hears of the legend of the night of the seventh moon “when mischief is abroad and is routed with the coming of dawn.” On one night, she gets lost in the mist of the forest and is rescued by a man who takes her to his hunting lodge. She taken with him that she might have allowed him to have his way with her but for the intervention of a housekeeper who took measures to preserve Helena’s virtue. But Helena never forgot the man even though she did not know his name.<br /><br />Years later, she returns to Germany and on another night of the seventh moon Helena meets and marries her German at his hunting lodge, but then she wakes from her idyllic honeymoon to discover she has been drugged by a physician who tells her she has escaped a horror that befell her in the forest. Helena lives in a fog of dreams and wonders where truth is.<br /><br />I have to say that I love Holt’s writing, and this story sucked me in immediately. It is labeled as a romantic suspense, but I didn’t see it containing any more suspense than many historical romances. But it does have a Gothic feel and there is a mystery. Holt had me wondering what had really happened. She did an excellent job of that. The book is a bit slow in the middle, and the hero and heroine are separated for years. In that interim, I found passages that seemed repetitive, but the ending is a great one. As always, Holt is a master storyteller and creates wonderfully vivid characters. <br /><br />I recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5421274472896597754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer620944415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13676767970042246927">I had never read a Victoria Holt book, and since there are so many, I chose the one that seemed to receive the best reviews. It was a quick summer read, but certainly not the page turner others described. I found several editing errors too which also served to distract. The characters were weak and ill defined. Those who were key were subject to the same foreshadowing inferences several times over. Her chosen settings were ripe for rich description, but again, Holt failed to hit the mark, only a</span>
  <span id="freeText13676767970042246927" style="display:none">I had never read a Victoria Holt book, and since there are so many, I chose the one that seemed to receive the best reviews. It was a quick summer read, but certainly not the page turner others described. I found several editing errors too which also served to distract. The characters were weak and ill defined. Those who were key were subject to the same foreshadowing inferences several times over. Her chosen settings were ripe for rich description, but again, Holt failed to hit the mark, only adequately describing both the prim British home and bookshop and the lush enchanted German forest. The plot was the best component, but so much more could have been made of it. I would give this novel a C, but I don't think I'll choose to read another book by this author.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2037277205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037277205" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5709636-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309315156p2/5709636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037277205?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/5709636-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385085793" href="/book/show/1327620.On_the_Night_of_the_Seventh_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5709636-anita?shelf=owned-print-book">owned-print-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5709636-anita?shelf=2017-halloween-bingo">2017-halloween-bingo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037277205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5079618329929536611"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I'm giving this book a very mid-ranged rating, because while it had a frustratingly over-dramatic romance, a frustratingly one-tracked heroine, and a frustratingly exasperating set of characters... well, the book was addictively engrossing.<br/><br/>I couldn't keep myself from wondering about what had happened to Helena, or what would happen to Helena... even while the entire ordeal was completely predictable.<br/><br/>I disliked a lot of the characters, and I disliked how blasé Frau Graber </span>
  <span id="freeText5079618329929536611" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br><br>I'm giving this book a very mid-ranged rating, because while it had a frustratingly over-dramatic romance, a frustratingly one-tracked heroine, and a frustratingly exasperating set of characters... well, the book was addictively engrossing.<br><br>I couldn't keep myself from wondering about what had happened to Helena, or what would happen to Helena... even while the entire ordeal was completely predictable.<br><br>I disliked a lot of the characters, and I disliked how blasé Frau Graber treated all the deaths, attempted murders, deception, lies, betrayals, and indifference of the nobility to these events; blowing them off as it being simply the culture in their country, and that everything was just about "state affair" and nothing to get worked up about. Boy, that was frustrating to get through that last half of the book.<br><br>Really, the only thing going for this book was the beautiful writing, the imagery, the description, and a lot of the lore and history laid within the book's world.<br><br>Anyway, I may or may not come back and give a proper review.<br><br>I read this book for <b>
  <a href="https://anicheungbookabyss.blogspot.com/p/halloween-bingo-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Halloween Bingo 2017</a>
</b>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505608842i/23940647.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5079618329929536611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2643382106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643382106" />
    <a title="Bookish Ally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66361703-bookish-ally"><img alt="Bookish Ally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550215017p2/66361703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643382106?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookish Ally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookish Ally" href="/user/show/66361703-bookish-ally">Bookish Ally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643382106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957403541565499030">Despite the 4stars (3.5, rounded up), I was disappointed by this book. The first half of the book did prove itself to buildup the atmosphere, which is so necessary to the gothic genre. I loved the idea of a story set in the land of fairy tales and legends, the dense old forests of Germany/Prussia. In many ways, Victoria creates a variation of fairytale by blending in some of the Nordic gods of old, and for that, plus the aforementioned atmospheric, she gets the higher marks. I didn’t care for th</span>
  <span id="freeText9957403541565499030" style="display:none">Despite the 4stars (3.5, rounded up), I was disappointed by this book. The first half of the book did prove itself to buildup the atmosphere, which is so necessary to the gothic genre. I loved the idea of a story set in the land of fairy tales and legends, the dense old forests of Germany/Prussia. In many ways, Victoria creates a variation of fairytale by blending in some of the Nordic gods of old, and for that, plus the aforementioned atmospheric, she gets the higher marks. I didn’t care for the two dimensional character development, but an exception given for her cranky aunts and the children’s nurse. Those two characters I really liked. 3.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9957403541565499030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oqtExGJ1QLCtKfR3dnkTIBTz1F+Rfzfj3I2WUHyabp535Hf+nwA2EZbPwvtjWLqKpkmFcbTOFjVQDI8e78ktVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rr0EhTg9F/pQqtvr7aG62bX/+slo+ovp2G663SuV+5h78je/xUhhW2tM7Wf4gBNzB0Wr501Lqj9U76OTuMa4UA==')})
  }

In a startling interview the master of the house, Brandon Reid, informs her that he wishes her to devote herself to moody, unbalanced Jeremy, Mrs. Reid\'s son by her previous husband, Brandon\'s younger brother Dwight. Dwight Reid\'s brilliant career as New York District Attorney had been ended by a shocking and tragic accident with a gun--or so the newspapers had claimed--at the hands of this same guilt-ridden child, then aged seven. Against her better judgment, Megan accepts the challenge.\n\nFrom the beginning Megan feels uneasy in the house; she senses the presence of lurking evil, of mysterious emotional undercurrents, of relationships that are not what they appear to be. She does not know whom to trust--the haughty yet strangely sad beauty, Leslie Reid, or the somber, fascinating master of the house, whose warm voice belies his cold, grave manner. She finds herself irresistibly drawn toward him, and their growing mutual attraction is duly noted by interested members of the household. When Megan realizes fully the extent of her own feelings, she knows she cannot honorably remain in the Reid home. <span id="freeTextContainer2419916044337385965"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/><br/>Eleanor Alice Burford, Mrs. George Percival Hibbert was a British author of about 200 historical novels, most of them under the pen name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6590.Jean_Plaidy' title='Jean Plaidy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jean Plaidy</a> which had sold 14 million copies by the time of her death. She chose to use various names because of the differences in subjec</span>
  <span id="freeText2419916044337385965" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />Eleanor Alice Burford, Mrs. George Percival Hibbert was a British author of about 200 historical novels, most of them under the pen name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6590.Jean_Plaidy" title="Jean Plaidy" rel="nofollow noopener">Jean Plaidy</a> which had sold 14 million copies by the time of her death. She chose to use various names because of the differences in subject matter between her books; the best-known, apart from Plaidy, are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25092.Victoria_Holt" title="Victoria Holt" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holt</a> (56 million) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/32.Philippa_Carr" title="Philippa Carr" rel="nofollow noopener">Philippa Carr</a> (3 million). Lesser known were the novels Hibbert published under her maiden name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1411371.Eleanor_Burford" title="Eleanor Burford" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor Burford</a>, or the pseudonyms of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2931390.Elbur_Ford" title="Elbur Ford" rel="nofollow noopener">Elbur Ford</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2931417.Kathleen_Kellow" title="Kathleen Kellow" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen Kellow</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1002136.Ellalice_Tate" title="Ellalice Tate" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellalice Tate</a>. Many of her readers under one penname never suspected her other identities.<br />-Wikipedia<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2419916044337385965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
